GT (fixed):  
\[
-0.2634379499\,v\sin(x)\;-\;0.5268758999\,v\;-\;2.5071295689\,x\;+\;0.4607662803\,\sin(t)
\]
So GT has exactly these structures: a linear-in-\(x\) term, a \(\sin(t)\) term with no exponential envelope, a linear-in-\(v\) term, and a mixed term \(v\sin(x)\). No \(x^2,x^3\), no \(v^2\) or \(v^3\), no \(v|v|\), no \(vx\), etc.

Key requirement: any matching candidate must be able (by choosing constants and possibly a domain restriction) to produce **both** \(v\sin(x)\) and \(v\) and \(x\) and \(\sin(t)\) with correct coefficients, and must not force extra nonzero functional forms.

### 49
Linear \(x\) and time sinusoid only; no \(v\sin(x)\) and no \(v\). ŌØī

### 50
Has \(\sin(c8 x+c9)\) inside the time-sinusoid factor (actually \(e^{c7 t}\sin(c8 x+c9)\)), which introduces \(x\)-dependent sinusoid not present in GTŌĆÖs \(\sin(t)\), and still no \(v\sin(x)\). ŌØī

---

**Conclusion:** None of the candidates contain (or can be tuned to contain) the essential mixed term \(v\sin(x)\). Domain restrictions like \(x\ge 0\) can help with Abs/Max forms, and phase shifts can convert sinŌåöcos, but they cannot create a missing multiplicative coupling \(v\sin(x)\) from purely additive separated terms.
